OF COOK COUNTY
Meeting of Tuesday, April 17, 2001
lO:OOA.M.
Daylight Saving Time

COOK COUNTY BOARD ROOM, COUNTY BUILDING

Board met pursuant to law and pursuant to Resolution Ol-R-12.

OFFICIAL RECORD
President Pro Tempore Lechowicz in the Chair.

CALL TO ORDER
At I 0:00 A.M., being the hour appointed for the meeting, the President Pro Tempore called the Board to
order.

QUORUM
County Clerk David Orr called the roll of members and there was found to be a quorum present.

ROLL CALL
Present:

Butler, Carr, Collins, Daley, Goslin, Hansen, Lechowicz, Maldonado, Moran, Moreno,
Quigley, Schumann, Silvestri, Sims, Steele, Sutker-16.

Absent:

Stroger-1 .

INVOCATION

Invocation.

committees.

various committee meetings.

President Pro Tempore Lechowicz in the Chair.

present~

Transmitting a Communication, dated April 12, 2001 from
TED LECHOWICZ, Chairman, Committee of Redistricting
requesting authorization for the execution of a personal service agreement with Ungaretti & Harris,
Chicago, Illinois, to assist the Redistricting Committee of the Cook County Board of Commissioners,
under the direction of the Chair of the Committee, or his designee, to perform the following services:
I.

research redistricting law and legal standards applicable to Cook County redistricting under
federal and Illinois constitutional and statutory requirements and case law principles, including
without limitation and Voting Rights Act and the right to use adjusted data, and update the same
for recent decisions;

2.

render advice and counsel to the Redistricting Committee regarding the foregoing and regarding
methods and approaches to redrawing of districts, appropriateness of use of particular data, use of
mapping and computer technology, coordination with election administration boundaries
(including precinct boundaries), and other issues relating to redistricting:

3.

monitor congressional, legislative, and City of Chicago remap proceedings;

4.

work with County staff and consultants to coordinate assembly of Census Bureau materials and
maps required or advisable for redistricting;

5.

attend meetings of the Redistricting Committee and of the Board of Commissioners as requested;
and

6.

perform such other work assignments relating to redistricting and to related laws and ordinances
as the Redistricting Committee might assign.

The fee for such proposal services would be $35,000. Such fee would be payable in progress payments as
follows:
$8,750

upon completion of four public hearings of the Redistricting Committee;

$8,750

upon completion of the final public hearing of the Redistricting Committee;

$8,750

upon completion of the initial map by the Redistricting Committee; and

$8,750

upon adoption of a final map by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR,
EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
TED LECHOWICZ, ROBERTO MALDONADO, WILLIAM R. MORAN,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI,
DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE and CAL VIN R. SUTKER, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

HONORING ANTHONY VACCO
EVERGREEN PARK MAYOR AND VILLAGE PRESIDENT 1968-2001
AND PRESIDENT OF THE SOUTHWEST COUNCIL OF MAYORS 1976-2001
WHEREAS, Evergreen Park Mayor Anthony Vacco has had a lifelong and distinguished career in public
service; and
WHEREAS, Anthony Vacco has served Evergreen Park as Building and Zoning Chairman (1961-1965),
as Trustee (1965-1968) and was appointed mayor in October 1968. He was elected to his first full fouryear term in 1969, and has been re-elected in each successive mayoral election since then, accumulating
service in that position for over thirty-two years; and
WHEREAS, under Mayor Vacco's accomplished leadership, steady guidance, and inspiring vision, the
Village of Evergreen Park, and indeed the whole southwest region of Cook County, has flourished and
prospered; and
WHEREAS, throughout his long tenure as Mayor and Village President, Anthony Vacco has always
been a steadfast and stalwart advocate for the people of his community and the people of Cook County.
In addition to his mayoral responsibilities he has been elected to and appointed to leadership positions in
the National League of Cities, the Illinois Municipal League, Cook County Solid Waste Disposal
Committee, the Council of Governments of Cook County, the Cook County Development Advisory
Council, the Southwest Council of Mayors and the Southwest Council of Local Governments; and

1357

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

WHEREAS, as Council Chairman for the Southwest Council of Mayors for the past twenty-five years,
Mayor Vacco has presided over a vast array of transportation concerns and improvements for the
southwest suburban Cook County region; and
WHEREAS, whether from a position of official prominence or as a member of the many organizations
he has been associated with, Anthony Vacco has conscientiously demonstrated his awareness of the issues
effecting the lives and well being of ordinary citizens, employing his determination and resolve to "get
the job done right" with courage, frankness, charm, and humor; and
WHEREAS, as a humanitarian and a man of faith, Anthony Vacco has given of his time and services
toward the improvement of the human condition and the betterment of the lives of individuals, not only in
Evergreen Park and Cook County, but for citizens throughout the State of Illinois and across our nation;
and
WHEREAS, Mayor Vacco, having decided not to seek a ninth full term as Evergreen Park Village
President, leaves those civic leaders remaining in public service proud to have known him and to have
served with him. His presence may be missed, but his many accomplishments will long be remembered.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Cook County Board
of Commissioners take this opportunity on behalf of the people of Cook County to express official
gratitude and deep appreciation to Mayor Anthony Vacco for his lifelong public service, dedication and
leadership; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official proceedings
of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, and that a copy thereof be tendered to Anthony Vacco as
a testimonial of the high esteem and appreciation in which he is regarded by the Members of the Board of
Commissioners of Cook County.

This item was WITHDRAWN at the request of the sponsor.

TERRY A. STECZO, Deputy Assessor for Administration & Intergovernmental Relations
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with SPSS, Inc., Chicago,
Illinois, for a twelve (12) user concurrent network license for computer software.
Reason:

The Assessor's Office uses SPSS, Inc. software primarily to do multiple regression analysis for
mass appraisal revaluation of residential properties. This software package allows users to
statically analyze the Assessor's Office's database. To allow additional functionality to the
Industrial/Commercial department, we are exchanging fifteen (l 5) user site licenses to a twelve
(12) user concurrent network license. This will allow better utilization of the software package.

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY
CAPITAL PROGRAM ITEMS

Transmitting a Communication, dated April 11, 2001 from
MICHAELE. LAMONT, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy
On August 4, 1999, the Honorable Board of Commissioners approved a Professional Services Agreement
between Cook County Court Associates and the County of Cook, for Program Management for the New
Traffic and Domestic Violence Court Project, which contract is identified as Contract No. 99-43-1437
(the "Contract"). The contract was amended by First Amendment authorized by the Board for execution
on December 5, 2000.
·
At its meeting of April 4, 2001, the Board took action evidencing its intent to terminate the process of
developing a New Traffic and Domestic Violence Court and cancel all contracts related to that process.
The contract entitles the County to terminate the contract for convenience at any time by notice in writing.
Authorization is therefore hereby requested for the Purchasing Agent to terminate the contract, as
amended, by appropriate written notice. Thereafter, the Office of Capital Planning and Policy will send
required notices and take such actions as are necessary to obtain delivery of all project documents, work
product and final billing and expense information so as to appropriately conclude this matter.
Authorization of the actions set forth above is respectfully requested.

Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the request of the Director of the
Office of Capital Planning and Policy be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

1380

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

01-R-252
RESOLUTION

Resolved that the President of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, on behalf of the
County of Cook, is hereby authorized and directed by the Members of said Board, to execute by original
signature or his authorized signature stamp, three (3) original copies of an Agreement with Consoer,
Townsend, Envirodyne Engineers, Inc. wherein the Consultant is to perform design engineering and
construction engineering for highway improvements at various locations under County of Cook jurisdiction
in the City of Chicago, said work to include preparation of reports, plans, special provisions, permits and
estimates for resurfacings, pavement rehabilitation, viaduct clearance improvements, signalizations,
streetscapings and other highway improvements, as well as provide construction inspection services which
include resident engineering, material testing, surveying and project documentation, all as directed by the
Highway Department and to be identified as Section: 01-8DECC-02-ES and it is further agreed, that the
County of Cook will reimburse Consoer, Townsend, Envirodyne Engineers, Inc. up to a maximum of SixHundred Thousand Dollars and No/100 ($600,000.00) for actual costs, said agreement submitted; and, the
Highway Department is authorized and directed to return an executed copy of this Resolution with
Agreement to the Consultant and implement the contract the Department's discretion.
April 17, 2001

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

STATE OF ILLINOIS
RESOLUTION FOR IMPROVEMENT BY COUNTY
UNDER THE ILLINOIS HIGHWAY CODE

BE IT RESOLVED, by the County Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, that the following
described County Highway be improved under the Illinois Highway Code:
County Highway W31, 84th Avenue, beginning at a point near 171 st Street and extending along said
route in a northerly direction to a point near 159th Street, a distance of approximately 1.52 miles; and

1381

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

existing pavement and shall include full depth patching, curb and gutter replacement, drainage additions
and replacements, traffic control, pavement marking, landscaping, engineering and other necessary
highway appurtenances and shall be designated as Section: 01-W3108-01-RS-MFT; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the improvement shall be constructed by contract; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of Two Hundred and TwentyFive Thousand and No/100 Dollars, ($225,000.00) from the County's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds
for the construction of this improvement; and

Resolution to the District Office of the Illinois Department of Transportation.
April 17, 2001

construction of Section: 93-W3210-02-RP of said County Highway; and
WHEREAS, the Resolution has been approved by the Department; and
WHEREAS, the County Board has adopted a Resolution stating that the public interest requires the
improvement of the above mentioned Section of the County Highway and has requested of the
Department that the County Highway be constructed and improved, as provided by law; and
WHEREAS, the Department did consider the desirability and importance of the proposed improvement
and determined that the construction will be practically possible; and
WHEREAS, the Department determined that the improvement will be of public utility and convenience
and after such consideration certified its approval of the proposed improvement to the Cook County
Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, having the Department's approval the Cook County Superintendent of Highways caused to
be , prepared proper surveys, maps, plans, specifications and estimates of cost of the proposed
improvement; and
WHEREAS, said plans and surveys require the private property be taken for such improvement pursuant
to authority granted under the 605 ILCS ( 1998) 5/5-801; and
WHEREAS, the private property to be taken consists of real property legally described in the exhibits
submitted herewith.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT, AND IT IS HEREBY RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners that the Cook County Superintendent of Highways is hereby authorized, empowered and
directed on behalf of the County of Cook to negotiate with the owner(s), and/or any parties of interest in the
property described herein, for the purpose of agreeing to the compensation to be paid for the property; and
IT IS HEREBY FURTHER RESOLVED, that in the event the parties cannot agree on the just
compensation to be paid for taking of the property, the State's Attorney for Cook County, Illinois shall
institute legal proceedings in a court of competent jurisdiction for the purpose of determining the just
compensation to be paid pursuant to the 735 ILCS (1998) 5/7-101. Furthermore, the State's Attorney is
authorized and directed to do any and all acts necessary and proper for the acquisition of the property
described herein.
April 17, 2001

Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Right-of-Way Land Acquisition
Resolution be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

AGREEMENT

Transmitting a Communication from
DONALD P. O'CONNELL, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
respectfully requests that the Board of Commissioners provide authorization for the County of Cook, on
behalf of the Circuit Court of Cook County, to enter into a proposed Stadium Rental Agreement ("the
Agreement") with the Illinois Sports Facilities Authority for the use of Comiskey Park facilities.
Although the cost of the Agreement is less than $10,000.00, this matter has been brought to your attention
on the advice of the Office of the State's Attorney, due specifically to the insurance and indemnification
provisions (see the Agreement, Section Five and Exhibit D). A representative of the Office of Risk
Management has approved the Agreement in its present form.

1387

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
Beginning on April~ 30, 2001, the Circuit Court of Cook County's Traffic Division will host the second
annual traffic safety initiative at Comiskey Park. The program, Smart Choices, will feature workshops,
demonstrations and a Driving Under the Influence (DUI) simulator to raise awareness among high school
students on the dangers of driving while intoxicated. More than 1,000 students from seventy Chicagoarea schools are expected to attend the five-day program. This initiative is an important part of the
court's comprehensive Drive Wise Stay Alive traffic safety awareness campaign, funded by a grant from
the Illinois Department of Transportation.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: $2,211.51. Contract period: April 30, 2001
through May 4, 2001. Requisition No. 18220015.

of the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved, as amended. The motion carried unanimously.

Court Reporter: Anthony Lisanti, C.S.R.
Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Finance of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice on
Wednesday, January 17, 2001, at the hour of 1:00 p.m. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building,
118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois, for the purpose of conducting public hearings regarding the
proposed Cook County Predatory Lending Ordinance.
240684

COOK COUNTY PREDATORY LENDING ORDINANCE (PROPOSED ORDINANCE).
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by John H. Stroger, Jr., President, Jerry Butler,
Allan C. Carr, Earlean Collins, John P. Daley, Gregg Goslin, Carl R. Hansen, Ted
Lechowicz, Roberto Maldonado, William R. Moran, Joseph Mario Moreno, Mike Quigley,
Herbert T. Schumann, Jr., Peter N. Silvestri, Deborah Sims, Bobbie L. Steele and Calvin R.
Sutker, County Commissioners.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the number of home mortgage foreclosures in Cook County has risen
dramatically over the last few years; and
WHEREAS, many homeowners in Cook County who lost their homes were victims of
predatory lenders. These lenders prey on unsuspecting, low-income borrowers by charging
exorbitantly high interest rates, fees and commissions, misrepresenting the mortgage terms
and engaging in other unfair and deceptive practices; and

1420

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

WHEREAS, those lenders who engage in the unscrupulous and unethical practice of
predatory lending strip hard earned equity from County residents and contribute to the
problems of vacant and abandoned houses and homelessness; and
WHEREAS, the Chairman of the Federal Reserve, the United States Congress, the United
States Department of Housing and Urban Development, Fannie Mae, various state
governments and the City of Chicago have recognized those abusive mortgage lending
practices which have led to the rising number of home foreclosures; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners calls upon the Attorney General of
Illinois to investigate and take legal action against predatory lenders; supports the Governor
of Illinois' initiatives against predatory lending; requests the Illinois General Assembly to
impose stricter regulations on mortgage lenders who engage in unfair and deceptive lending
practices; asks that community and religious leaders establish educational programs that will
alert consumers to the dangers of predatory lending and directs the Chief Financial Officer of
Cook County to make appropriate recommendations in regard to any financial institution
engaged in predatory lending which seeks a County contract or designation as a County
depository.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF
THE COUNTY OF COOK, ILLINOIS, AS FOLLOWS:
SECTION 1
SECTION 2
SECTION 3
SECTION 4
SECTION 5
SECTION 6

TITLE
DEFINITIONS
COUNTY CONTRACTS
COUNTY DEPOSITORIES
SEVERABILITY
EFFECTIVE DATE

240684

COOK COUNTY PREDATORY LENDING ORDINANCE (PROPOSED ORDINANCE).

PROPOSED ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the number of home mortgage foreclosures in Cook County has nsen
dramatically over the last few years; and
WHEREAS, many homeowners in Cook County who lost their homes were victims of
predatory lenders. These lenders prey on unsuspecting, low-income borrowers by charging

and engaging in other unfair and deceptive practices; and
WHEREAS, those lenders who engage in the unscrupulous and unethical practice of

WHEREAS, the Chairman of the Federal Reserve, the United States Congress, the United
States Department of Housing and Urban Development, Fannie Mae, various state
governments and the City of Chicago have recognized those abusive mortgage lending
practices which have led to the rising number of home foreclosures; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners calls upon the Attorney General of

Chairman Daley stated the Finance Committee has held four public hearings throughout the County in
reference to the (proposed) Cook County Predatory Lending Ordinance.
Chairman Daley entered into the record the eighteen amendments that have been proposed by the
members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners to the Cook County Predatory Lending Ordinance
(#240684).
Following testimony, the Committee commenced consideration of the amendments:

AMENDMENT #1
Sponsors:

President John H. Stroger, Jr.
Commissioner John P. Daley

Co-Sponsors: Commissioners Jerry Butler, Allan C. Carr, Earlean Collins, Gregg Goslin, Carl R.
Hansen, Ted Lechowicz, Roberto Maldonado, William R. Moran, Joseph Mario
Moreno, Mike Quigley, Herbert T. Schumann, Jr., Peter N. Silvestri, Deborah Sims,
Bobbie L. Steele and Calvin R. Sutker
Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
This language clarifies the basis of the County's local governmental interest in declining to contract with
predatory lenders.

Adds: New Whereas clause, following the third recital.
WHEREAS, the Co unty desires to promote the public interesL and to d i courage predato1y
lending practices within Cook County by declining o enter into contracts with predatory lenders and

thereby conferring financial benefits upon those lenders.
Leave was granted to add all members as co-sponsors.

Sponsors:

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
This amendment substitutes the word "financial" for the word "tangible" for the purpose of specificity
and clarification.

Amends:

Section 2 - Definitions: "Flipping"

"Flipping" means the refinancing and charging of additional points, charges or other costs on a
threshold loan within a 24 month period after the refinanced loan was made, unless the refinancing results
in a t8:8gible financial benefit to the borrower.

Amends:

Section 2 - Definitions: "Predatory lender"

"Predatory lender" means a financial institution that has made, within the pre'+'io1:1s 12 month
period, prioi" to ubrni sion of a bid or contract offer, or prior to the date of propo ed designation as a
County depository, whichever is applicable, predatory loans that comprise either: (1) 5% of the total
annual number of loans made, or (2) 25 individual loans; whichever is less. Each financial institution and
affiliate shall be considered separately for the purposes of these calculations, and only loans secured by
residential real estate that is located within the County shall be considered. The term "predatory lender"
shall not include a financial institution, or its affiliates, that has submitted to the Chief Financial Officer a
plan which is accepted in writing by the Chief Financial Officer to discontinue the practice of making
predatory loans which plan, if the plan ens1:1res: (i) ensures the prompt disengagement from the practice of
making predatory loans by the financial institution and its affiliates, and (ii) ensures the complete
cessation of the making of predatory loans by the financial institution and its affiliates within 180 days
after the plan is submitted; provided that no more than one plan may be submitted on behalf of any
financial institution.

lender may result in the loss of the privilege of doing business with the
County.

AMENDMENT #6
Sponsors:

President John H. Stroger, Jr.
Commissioner John P. Daley

Co-Sponsors:

Commissioners Allan C. Carr, Gregg Goslin, Carl R. Hansen, Ted Lechowicz, William
R. Moran, Joseph Mario Moreno, Herbert T. Schumann, Jr., Deborah Sims, Bobbie L.
Steele and Calvin R. Sutker

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
This amendment substitutes the word "may" for "will" so as to ensure that the Treasurer has flexibility in
the matter of County depositories.

Amends:
B.

Section 4 - County Depositories (B)
Upon receipt of any written complaint regarding predatory lending practices by any financial
institution seeking designation as a County depository or serving as a County depository, the
Chief Financial Officer shall refer such complaints to the Treasurer who will may conduct an
investigation of the complaint in accordance with the Treasurer's policies and procedures.

Leave was granted to add Commissioners Carr, Goslin, Hansen, Lechowicz, Moran, Moreno, Schumann,
Sims, Steele and Sutker as co-sponsors.
Commissioner Silvestri asked if the change in the language of the ordinance, from "will" to "may" is
consistent with the City of Chicago ordinance? He stated the change in terminology will make the
Treasurer's action discretionary.
Chairman Daley responded he believes the language is consistent with the City of Chicago ordinance and
was recommended by the State's Attorney's Office.
Commissioner Lechowicz stated that it was explained to him that the reason for the amendment is
because the County cannot dictate these actions to the Treasurer.
Chairman Daley asked Helen Haynes, Assistant State's Attorney, to address the Committee.
ASA Haynes stated the change in language was recommended in light of the statutes governing the
County Treasurer, and the County Treasurer's discretion in recommending the designation of the County
depository. She continued by stating that it would be more consistent with the statutory authority granted
to the Treasurer if this were something that was transmitted to the Treasurer, where she may then
investigate and take action.

1431

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
Commissioner Silvestri stated his concern ifthe County Treasurer was not willing to work with the Board
of Commissioners, that person would then have the ability to circumvent the purpose of the ordinance.
He indicated that the elected Board of Commissioners should have some authority over the operations of
one of the offices that it funds. He indicated he understands the division of powers and how statutory
authority is given to various elected offices. However, he stated he does not think the Legislature
intended other County elected officials to be totally free from any control exercised by the Board of
Commissioners.
Commissioner Silvestri asked what would happen if this amendment is not approved?
ASA Haynes indicated there could be a Treasurer that objects to the originally proposed language and
takes legal action by suing the Board. In response to Commissioner Lechowicz, ASA Haynes stated she
would provide a briefing on the statutes that govern the Treasurer's authority regarding the issue of
County depositories.
Commissioner Lechowicz remarked that the State has eminent domain on this issue. He said the statutes
are clear as far as certain County offices are concerned as well as the responsibility of the County Board
to that office, and that office to the State of Illinois.
Commissioner Hansen stated the Home Rule powers of the County do not take precedence over the
constitutional powers of the Treasurer. He said the language should be optional so that the County Board
does not run afoul of the constitutional duties of the Treasurer.
Commissioner Butler stated he does not believe that the Treasurer, who is the custodian of the funds, has
powers that supercede that of the Board in terms of where the funds should be deposited. He agrees with
Commissioner Silvestri in that the word "may" leads to ambiguity.
Commissioner Maldonado also agreed with Commissioner Silvestri that the word "may" is too
discretionary, giving the option and subjective discretion to the Treasurer to act upon this or not. He
asked why the State's Attorney's Office suggested the word "may".
ASA Haynes responded that there is one specific statute that allows the Treasurer to request the County
Board to designate a depository, as referenced in sub-point A of Section 4 of the Ordinance. However, in
the instances in which the Treasurer is independently exercising her general constitutional and statutory
authority over funds, there may be a potential problem by directing the Treasurer in a certain manner.
Commissioner Maldonado stated if the ordinance is adopted with the term "will", it is suggested that the
Treasurer has the option of not having to comply with the language of this ordinance. He asked where the
Home Rule power of this County lies?
ASA Haynes responded the powers granted to the County have to be taken in the context of the powers
granted to individually elected officials as well as those provided by statute under the body of law in the
Constitution. She recommended this language be considered as being more consistent with existing law.
Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Vice Chairman Carr, moved approval of Amendment #6.
Commissioner Butler called for a Roll Call, the vote of yeas and nays being as follows:

1432

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

ROLL CALL ON MOTION TO APPROVE AMENDMENT #6
Yeas:

Vice Chairman Carr, Chairman Daley, Commissioners Goslin, Hansen, Lechowicz,
Moran, Sims and Steele (8)

Nays:

Commissioners Butler, Collins, Maldonado, Quigley and Silvestri (5)

Absent:

Commissioners Moreno, Schumann, Sutker and President Stroger (4)

The motion to approve Amendment #6 CARRIED.

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
Administrative rules can significantly change the intent of any ordinance. Having such rules reviewed by
the County Board will help prevent such changes from happening.

(11)

Section 2 - Definitions: "Predatory Loan" (11)
Such other circumstances that the Chief Financial Officer may determine to be predatory
in nature, in administrative rules promulgated to implement this Ordinance, which rules

SUBSTITUTE AMENDMENT #8
Sponsor:

Commissioner Carl R. Hansen

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
Previous language allows lender to escape the intent of the ordinance through widely varying
interpretations of the words "reasonably believe."

Amends:

Section 2 - Definitions: "Predatory Loan" (8)

1433

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

(8)

Lending without due regard to repayment ability: The lender makes a loan if the lender 0ees
n.ot reason~ believe~ at the time the loan is consummated that the borrower or the
borrowers (when considered collectively in the case of multiple borrowers) will not be able to
make the scheduled payments to repay the obligation based upon a consideration of their
current and expected income, current obligations, employment status, and other financial
resources (other than the borrower's equity in the dwelling which secures repayment of the
loan). A borrower shall be presumed to be able to make the scheduled payments to repay the
obligation if, at the time the loan is consummated, or at the time of the first rate adjustment in
the case of a lower introductory interest rate, the borrower's scheduled monthly payments on
the loan (including principal, interest, taxes, insurance and assessments), combined with the
scheduled payments for all other debts, do not exceed 50% of the borrower's monthly gross
income as verified by the credit application, the borrower's financial statement, a credit
report, financial information provided to the lender by or on behalf of the borrower, or any
other reasonable means. This provision applies only to borrowers whose income, as reported
on the loan application which the lender relied upon in making the credit decision, is no
greater than 120% of the median family income for the Chicago Metropolitan Statistical Area
(MSA) (as defined by the Director of the U.S. Office of Management and Budget). For
purposes of this Ordinance, the median family income shall be derived from the most recent
estimates made available by the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development, at the
time the application is received. For purposes of determining median income, only the
income of the borrower or borrowers shall be considered;

Chairman Daley announced that a substitute amendment had been previously distributed.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved approval of Substitute
Amendment #8. The motion carried. Commissioner Moran voted no.
AMENDMENT #9
Sponsor:

Commissioner Peter N. Silvestri

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
Most homeowners will need to refinance out of their predatory loans. Thus far, only Harris Bank and
Fannie Mae have developed an alternative product to help those in the midst of a predatory loan. This
alternative product pays off the predatory loan and replaces it with a more conventional loan.

Amends:

Section 2 - Definitions: "Predatory lender"

"Predatory lender" means a financial institution that has made, within the previous 12 month
period, predatory loans that comprise either: (1) 5% of the total annual number of loans made, or (2) 25
individual loans; whichever is less. Each financial institution and affiliate shall be considered separately
for the purposes of these calculations, and only loans secured by residential real estate that is located
within the County shall be considered. The term "predatory lender" shall not include a financial
institution, or its affiliates, that has submitted to the Chief Financial Officer a plan which is accepted in
writing by the Chief Financial Officer to discontinue the practice of making predatory loans, if.the which
plan ensures: (i) the prompt disengagement from the practice of making predatory loans by the financial
institution and its affiliates, aft0 (ii) the complete cessation of the making of predatory loans by the
financial institution and its affiliates within 180 days after the plan is submitted; and (iii) development of
an alternative non-predatory loan product to help finance borrowers out of predatory loans; provided that
no more than one plan may be submitted on behalf of any financial institution.

Amendment #9 was withdrawn at the request of the sponsor.

1434

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

AMENDMENT #10
Sponsor:

Commissioner Peter N. Silvestri

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
If a HUD 1 Settlement Paper and Truth in Lending documents are attached to foreclosure filings,
homeowners may be able to use the Illinois Interest Act as a defense, which would put a moratorium on
their foreclosure until that suit is settled.

Amends:

5th Whereas clause

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners calls upon the Attorney General of
Illinois to investigate and take legal action against predatory lenders; supports the Governor of Illinois'
initiatives against predatory lending; requests the Illinois General Assembly to impose stricter regulations
on mortgage lenders who engage in unfair and deceptive lending practices; requests the Illinois General
Assembly to require a HUD 1 Settlement Paper and Trutll in Lendi11g documents be attached to aU
foreclosure filings; asks that community and religious leaders establish educational programs that will
alert consumers to the dangers of predatory lending and directs the Chief Financial Officer of Cook
County to make appropriate recommendations in regard to any financial institution engaged in predatory
lending which seeks a County contract or designation as a County depository;

Amendment #10 was withdrawn at the request of the sponsor.

Leave was granted to add Commissioners Butler and Collins as co-sponsors.
Commissioner Quigley stated that he is aware the Board cannot regulate the insurance business, and this
amendment does not attempt to do so. The Commissioner said the ordinance addresses the mortgage
industry in the same way that it addresses the insurance industry. He said the Federal Reserve Board has
now recommended that the financing of credit life can be included in points and fees. He stated that
Governor Ryan's proposed regulations not only included credit life in the definition of points and fees,
but prohibits the sale of lump sum credit life in high cost loans. The Commissioner further stated that
Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac both refuse to purchase subprime loans that include single premium credit
insurance, and a joint report by HUD and the U.S. Treasury recommends banning this type of product
altogether.
Commissioner Lechowicz stated that amendment #12 effectively bans single premium credit life
insurance. He said this amendment differs from the City's ordinance and would impose very different
requirements on the same lenders governing the same loans. He indicated that the City of Chicago is
going to address this issue, and when the State's Joint Committee on Administrative Rules (JCAR) rules
on the matter, the Board could follow suit. He indicated that the Board should not act prematurely but
should wait to make sure that the State takes the appropriate lead in this critical area. He requested that a
Chicago Tribune article dated March 31, 2001, by Melissa Allison be entered into the record. The article
concerns Governor Ryan's revised rules on lending.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved approval of Amendment #12.
The motion to approve Amendment #12 FAILED. Commissioner Butler, Collins and Quigley voted
yes, and Commissioner Silvestri voted present.
AMENDMENT #13
Sponsor:

Commissioner Mike Quigley

Co-Sponsor:

Leave was granted to add Commissioner Butler as a co-sponsor.
Commissioner Quigley stated the amendment follows the recommendations that Governor Ryan and the
Federal Reserve Board have made. The amendment informs citizens that the Board of Commissioners is
concerned about the growing number of foreclosures. He noted the ordinance includes credit life in the
definition of points and fees.
Commissioner Maldonado defined a predatory loan as a threshold loan, that has charges in terms of points
exceeding five percent. He stated the public has testified at the hearings, that most lenders sell single
premium life insurance and share fees with either the broker or lender. As an example, the Commissioner
said if the lender charges $5000 for the premium and it is split with the broker, that means the lender is
charging five points, plus $2500, which on a $100,000 loan means an additional two and half points in
terms of fees. He stated his concern that if the amendment is not approved, there will be more
proliferation of credit life insurance pushed on customers. He supports the adoption of the amendment.
Commissioner Collins stated that the ordinance is not to regulate all banks and financial institutions in
Cook County, but to regulate a few banks where the County has deposits.
Commissioner Lechowicz indicated that the County does not have the authority to regulate certain
institutions. He stated it is the province of the State and that the Joint Committee on Administrative Rules
can address this issue. He noted that adoption of the amendment would be premature.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved approval of Amendment
#13. Commissioner Quigley called for a Roll Call, the vote of yeas and nays being as follows:

AMENDMENT #15
Sponsor:

Commissioner Roberto Maldonado

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
The "yield spread premium" available to mortgage brokers from lenders is currently included in the APR
(annual percentage rate) calculation. If this premium is also included in the points and fees test, the
amount will be double counted and not representative of the actual APR.

Amends:

Section 2 - Definitions: "Points and fees" (3)

(3)
All compensation paid directly or indirectly to a mortgage broker, including a broker that
originates a loan in its own name in a table funded transaction, not otherwise included in paragraph (1) or
(2) of this subdivision, but not including any yield spread premium paid to a mortgage broker if the
premium is reflected in the annual percentage rate of the loan;

Amendment #15 was withdrawn at the request of the sponsor.

The fees the title company charges for conducting the closing at their office are third party fees ("bona

broker or an affiliate of the mortgage broker.")

Amends:

is given the option to obtain the service or product from an unaffiliated entity.

AMENDMENT #17
Sponsor:

Commissioner Carl R. Hansen

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
Recommendation of the State's Attorney without which the Ordinance may be vulnerable to challenge as
infringing upon the Treasurer's authority.

Amends:

Section 4 (A) - County Depositories

SECTION 4 - COUNTY DEPOSITORIES
A.

All financial institutions, seeking designation as a County depository by the Board of
Commissioners upon the request of the Treasurer, shall submit to the Chief Financial Officer,
prior to any such designation, a pledge affirming that neither it nor any of its affiliates is or
will become a predatory lender within the County. Upon receipt, the Chief Financial Officer
shall forward this pledge to the Treasurer. The pledge shall be signed by the chairman of the
board, chief executive officer, or other officer of the financial institution acceptable to the
Chief Financial Officer. The pledge shall be in substantially the following form:
We pledge that we are not and will not become a predatory lender as defined in this
Ordinance. We further pledge that none of our affiliates is, and none of them will become, a
predatory lender as defined in this Ordinance. We understand that becoming a predatory
lender or becoming an affiliate of a predatory lender may result in the loss of our designation
as a County depository.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved approval of Amendment #17.
The motion carried.

Commissioner Collins indicated Amendment #18 puts the responsibility on the mortgage broker or the
lender. The Commissioner said there are specific rules, practices and procedures that must be followed
to determine whether or not a person can afford to repay the loan, especially when one looks at home
equity loans to ensure that people do not lose their property. The Commissioner said the Amendment
requires the lender to certify the person and to determine that the borrower has the financial ability to pay
the loan in accordance with the terms of the loan. She indicated that the borrower will receive a copy of
the certification signed by the mortgagor saying that they have validated the fact that this person has the
financial ability to repay the loan.
Commissioner Lechowicz asked ASA Haynes if she had an opportunity to review Amendment # 18?

1440

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
ASA Haynes answered that she did review Amendment # 18 and appreciates the concern it addresses. She
said the State has a broader ability to regulate the practice of banking and that this amendment would
appear to impose an affirmative requirement that lenders enter into a certification that the borrower has
the ability to repay the loan. From a legal standpoint, ASA Haynes indicated that it may appear to be
regulating banking in a manner that goes beyond the County's authority. She indicated there are no real
criteria set forth in this ordinance by which a lender can make that certification. She indicated there are
general standards out there and did not know whether or not it is currently widespread practice to make a
certification like this. She did not think such standards are set forth in the amendment. ASA Haynes also
stated there is a significant issue as to whether or not the County may be going a step beyond what the
ordinance intends.
Commissioner Collins said the intent of the amendment is to certify and validate that the borrower's
income can support the mortgage payments.
Ms. Haynes indicated the amendment seeks general certification and one that is keyed to a specific
Federal law. She said it imposes an affirmative obligation upon the lender and would declare that a
mortgage, which was issued and for which the borrower did not financially qualify, would appear to have
been issued under fraudulent terms, which is a statement that may go beyond what actually happened.
ASA Haynes commented that under the amendment, the mortgage would be deemed null and void. Ms.
Haynes concluded that she does not think the County Board can promulgate an ordinance that would have
the authority to declare a mortgage null and void.
Commissioner Lechowicz advised the committee to follow the Assistant State's Attorney's advice that
the County Board does not have certain jurisdictional powers over financial institutions in this County or
State. He said he had serious reservations and did not think this amendment should be considered at this
time, based upon the State's Attorney's recommendation.
Commissioner Steele concurred with Commissioner Lechowicz and indicated that the State has greater
powers than Cook County.
Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved approval of Amendment #18.
Commissioner Collins called for a Roll Call, the vote of yeas and nays being as follows:
ROLL CALL ON MOTION TO APPROVE AMENDMENT #18
Yeas:

Commissioners Collins and Quigley (2)

Nays:

Commissioner Butler, Chairman Daley, Commissioners Goslin, Hansen, Lechowicz,
Maldonado, Moran, Silvestri and Sims (9)

Present:

Commissioner Steele (1)

Absent:

Vice Chairman Carr, Commissioners Moreno, Schumann, Sutker and President
Stroger (5)

The motion to approve Amendment #18 FAILED.
Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Cook County
Predatory Lending Ordinance (Item 240684) be approved and adopted, as amended.
Commissioner Lechowicz called for a Roll Call, the vote of yeas and nays being as follows:

01-0-7
ORDINANCE

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
COOK COUNTY PREDATORY LENDING ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the number of home mortgage foreclosures in Cook County has risen dramatically
over the last few years; and
WHEREAS, many homeowners in Cook County who lost their homes were victims of predatory
lenders. These lenders prey on unsuspecting, low-income borrowers by charging exorbitantly high
interest rates, fees and commissions, misrepresenting the mortgage terms and engaging in other unfair and
deceptive practices; and
WHEREAS, those lenders who engage in the unscrupulous and unethical practice of predatory
lending strip hard earned equity from County residents and contribute to the problems of vacant and
abandoned houses and homelessness; and
WHEREAS, the County desire. to promote the public interest and to discourage predatory
lending practices within Cook Co unty by declining t0 enter in to contracts with predatory I.end ers and
thereby conferring financial benefits upon those lenders; and
WHEREAS, the Chairman of the Federal Reserve, the United States Congress, the United States
Department of Housing and Urban Development, Fannie Mae, various state governments and the City of
Chicago have recognized those abusive mortgage lending practices which have led to the rising number
of home foreclosures; and

1442

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners calls upon the Attorney General of
Illinois to investigate and take legal action against predatory lenders; supports the Governor of Illinois'
initiatives against predatory lending; requests the Illinois General Assembly to impose stricter regulations
on mortgage lenders who engage in unfair and deceptive lending practices; asks that community and
religious leaders establish educational programs that will alert consumers to the dangers of predatory
lending and directs the Chief Financial Officer of Cook County to make appropriate recommendations in
regard to any financial institution engaged in predatory lending which seeks a County contract or
designation as a County depository;
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF THE COUNTY
OF COOK, ILLINOIS, AS FOLLOWS:
SECTION 1 - TITLE

This Ordinance shall be known as the "Cook County Predatory Lending Ordinance."
SECTION 2 - DEFINITIONS

For purposes of this Ordinance, whenever any of the following words, terms or definitions are
used, they shall have the meaning ascribed to them in this section:
"Affiliate" means any entity that controls, is controlled by, or is under common control with
another entity, as determined under the federal Bank Holding Company Act of 1956, as amended from
time to time. However, "affiliate" specifically shall not include any entity whose predominant business is
the providing of tax deferred, defined contribution, pension plans to public employees in accordance with
Sections 403(b) and 457 of the Internal Revenue Code.
"Chief Financial Officer" means the Chief Financial Officer of Cook County.
"Financial Institution" means a bank, savings and loan association, thrift, credit union, mortgage
banker, mortgage broker, a trust company, a savings bank, an investment bank, a securities broker, a
municipal securities broker, a securities dealer, a municipal securities dealer, a securities underwriter, a
municipal securities underwriter, an investment trust, a venture capital company, a bank holding
company, a financial services holding company, or any licensee under the Consumer Installment Loan
Act, the Sales Finance Agency Act, or the Residential Mortgage Licensing Act. However, "financial
institution" specifically shall not include any entity whose predominant business is the providing of tax
deferred, defined contribution, pension plans to public employees in accordance with Sections 403(b) and
457 of the Internal Revenue Code.
"First lien mortgage" means any loan secured by a first lien on residential real property, including
but not limited to purchase money and non-purchase money loans, refinancing loans, home equity loans,
and reverse mortgages.
"Flipping" means the refinancing and charging of additional points, charges or other costs on a
threshold loan within a 24 month period after the refinanced loan was made, unless the refinancing results
in a ta-ngible financial benefit to the borrower.
"Home equity loan" means the extension of credit secured by a leOOef lien on residential real
propertv under a plan in which:
(I)

The lender reasonably contemplates repeated transactions;

1443

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
(2)

The lender may impose a finance charge from time to time on an outstanding balance; and

(3) The amount of credit that may be extended to the borrower during the term of the plan (up
to any limit set by the lender) is generally made available to the extent that any outstanding balance is
repaid.
"Junior mortgage" means any loan secured by a mortgage other than a first lien mortgage.
"Points and fees" means:
(1) All items required to be disclosed under sections 226.4(a) and 226.4(b) of Title 12 of the
Code of Federal Regulations, as amended from time to time, except the interest rate or time-price
differential;
(2) Subject to the exclusions provided below in this subdivision, all charges for items listed
under section 226.4( c)(7) of Title 12 of the Code of Federal Regulations, as amended from time to time,
but only if the lender receives direct or indirect compensation, in connection with the charge or the charge
is paid to an affiliate of the lender, and otherwise the charges are not included within the meaning of the
phrase "points and fees";
(3) All compensation paid directly or indirectly to a mortgage broker, including a broker that
originates a Joan in its own name in a table funded transaction, not otherwise included in paragraph (1) or
(2) of this subdivision;
(4) The premium of any single premium credit life, credit disability, credit unemployment, or
any other life or health insurance that is financed directly or indirectly into the loan, unless the disclosures
and acknowledgment described in predatory loan practice (7) below have been made.
"Points and fees" shall not include: (i) taxes, filing fees, recording and other charges and fees
paid or to be paid to public officials for determining the existence of or for perfecting, releasing or
satisfying a security interest; (ii) a payment to a government agency or a government-sponsored agency in
connection with a government-sponsored mortgage program; (iii) bona fide and reasonable fees paid to a
person other than a lender or an affiliate of the lender or to the mortgage broker or an affiliate of the
mortgage broker for the following: fees for tax payment services; fees for 'flood certification; fees for pest
infestation and flood determinations; appraisal fees; fees for home inspections performed prior to closing;
credit reports; surveys; attorney's fees (if the borrower has the right to select the attorney); notary fees;
escrow charges, so long as not otherwise included under paragraph (1) of this subdivision; title insurance
premiums; and hazard insurance and flood insurance premiums, provided that the conditions in section
226.4(d)(2) of Title 12 of the Code of Federal Regulations, as amended from time to time, are met; and
(iv) any bona fide, competitive and reasonable fees paid to the lender or an affiliate of the lender for the
services and products described in clause (iii), but only if the loan is not conditioned on the fees being
paid to the lender or its affiliate, and the borrower is given the option to obtain the service or product from
an unaffiliated entity.
"Predatory lender" means a financial institution that has made, within the pre·Aous 12 month
period, prior to submiss i n of a bid or contract offer. or prior to the date of proposed designation as a
County depository, whichever is applicable, predatory loans that comprise either: (1) 5% of the total
annual number of loans made, or (2) 25 individual loans; whichever is less. Each financial institution and
affiliate shall be considered separately for the purposes of these calculations, and only Joans secured by
residential real estate that is located within the County shall be considered. The term "predatory lender"
shall not include a financial institution, or its affiliates, that has submitted to the Chief Financial Officer a

1444

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

plan which is accepted in writing by the Chief Financial Officer to discontinue the practice of making
predatory loans which plan, if the plaTl ensl:lres: (i) ensures the prompt disengagement from the practice
of making predatory loans by the financial institution and its affiliates, and (ii) ensures the complete
cessation of the making of predatory loans by the financial institution and its affiliates within 180 days
after the plan is submitted; provided that no more than one plan may be submitted on behalf of any
financial institution.
"Predatory loan" means a threshold loan that was made under circumstances that involve any of
the following acts or practices:
(1)

Fraudulent or deceptive acts or practices, including fraudulent or deceptive marketing and
sales efforts to sell threshold loans.

(2)

Prepayment penalties: (i) that apply to a prepayment made after the expiration of the 36
month period following the date the loan was made, or (ii) that are more than 3% of the
total loan amount if the prepayment is made within the first 12 month period following the
date the loan was made, or more than 2% of the total loan amount if the prepayment is
made within the second 12 month period after the date the loan was made, or more than l %
of the loan amount if the prepayment is made within the third 12 month period following
the date the loan was made.

(3)

Balloon payments: A threshold loan that has a payment schedule with regular periodic
payments that when aggregated do not fully amortize the outstanding principal balance,
except for bridge loans connected with the acquisition or construction of a dwelling
intended to become the borrower's principal dwelling, and except for loans with a final
balloon payment that have a term of not less than 180 months provided such balloon
payment is conspicuously disclosed to the borrower, and except for home equity loans.

(4)

Loan flipping.

(5)

Negative amortization: A threshold loan, other than a loan secured only by a reverse
mortgage, with terms under which the outstanding balance will increase at any time over
the course of the loan because the regular periodic payments do not cover the full amount
of the interest due, unless the negative amortization is the consequence of a temporary
forbearance sought by the borrower.

( 6)

The financing of points and fees in excess of 6% of the loan amount.

(7)

The financing of a single premium credit life, credit disability, credit unemployment, or any
other life or health insurance, directly or indirectly, into one or more threshold loans unless
the lender, at least three business days before the borrower signs the loan agreement, makes
to the borrower a separate oral disclosure, and a separate clear and conspicuous written
disclosure containing the following information, all of which must be true: (i) the total cost
of the insurance premium and, separately stated, the total amount of interest that will be
charged for the financing of the insurance premium over the life of the loan; (ii) the fact
that the insurance will be prepaid and financed at the interest rate provided for in the loan;
(iii) the fact that the purchase of such insurance is not required in order to obtain the loan;
(iv) the amount that the lender or its affiliates will receive as direct or indirect commissions
in connection with the insurance; (v) that the borrower may terminate the insurance at any
time and receive a refund of the unearned premium, and that the borrower will receive a
refund of the entire premium if the borrower cancels the insurance within 90 days after the

1445

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

policy goes into effect; (vi) the term of the insurance coverage and, if different from the
term of the loan, the length of the difference. In addition, the written disclosure shall
contain a signed and dated acknowledgment by the borrower that the oral disclosure was
made, and a signed and dated acknowledgment by the lender that the oral disclosure was
made.
(8)

Lending without due regard to repayment ability: The lender makes a loan if the lender
does Rot reasoRa9ly believe~ at the time the loan is consummated that the borrower or the
borrowers (when considered collectively in the case of multiple borrowers) will not be able
to make the scheduled payments to repay the obligation based upon a consideration of their
current and expected income, current obligations, employment status, and other financial
resources (other than the borrower's equity in the dwelling which secures repayment of the
loan). A borrower shall be presumed to be able to make the scheduled payments to repay
the obligation if, at the time the loan is consummated, or at the time of the first rate
adjustment in the case of a lower introductory interest rate, the borrower's scheduled
monthly payments on the loan (including principal, interest, taxes, insurance and
assessments), combined with the scheduled payments for all other debts, do not exceed
50% of the borrower's monthly gross income as verified by the credit application, the
borrower's financial statement, a credit report, financial information provided to the lender
by or on behalf of the borrower, or any other reasonable means. This provision applies
only to borrowers whose income, as reported on the loan application which the lender
relied upon in making the credit decision, is no greater than 120% of the median family
income for the Chicago Metropolitan Statistical Area (MSA) (as defined by the Director of
the U.S. Office of Management and Budget). For purposes of this Ordinance, the median
family income shall be derived from the most recent estimates made available by the U.S.
Department of Housing and Urban Development, at the time the application is received.
For purposes of determining median income, only the income of the borrower or borrowers
shall be considered;

(9)

The payment by a lender to a contractor under a home improvement contract from the
proceeds of a threshold loan, other than:
(i)

by an instrument payable to the borrower or jointly to the borrower and the contractor;
or

(ii) at the election of the borrower, by a third party escrow agent in accordance with terms
established in a written agreement signed by the borrower, the lender, and the
contractor before the date of payment;
( 10) The payment from loan proceeds by a lender to a contractor under a home repair or
improvement contract, where the contractor has been, on two or more occasions within the
previous 24 month period, determined by a court or agency of competent jurisdiction to be
in violation of any law or ordinance prohibiting deceptive practices or similar conduct,
unless: (i) the lender has no knowledge of the determinations, and (ii) the lender has
received a written affidavit from the contractor stating that there have not been two or more
such determinations regarding the contractor within the previous 24 month period.
(11) Such other circumstances that the Chief Financial Officer may determine to be predatory in
nature, in administrative rules promulgated to implement this Ordinance, which rules shall
be submitted to the Cook County Board of Commissioners for their approval.

1446

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

"Reverse mortgage" means a nonrecourse security interest in the borrower's principal dwelling
where no interest or principal is payable on the secured loan (except in the case of default) until: (i) the
borrower dies; (ii) the dwelling is transferred; or (iii) the borrower ceases to occupy the dwelling.
"Threshold loan" means a loan that is entered into after the effective date of this Ordinance and is
secured by residential real property located within the County on which there is situated a dwelling for
not more than four families or a condominium unit, or is secured by a cooperative unit within the County,
if:
(1)
at the time of the loan's origination, the annual percentage rate of the loan exceeds by
more than 6 percentage points in the case of a first lien mortgage, or by more than 8 percentage points in
the case of a junior mortgage, the yield on Treasury securities having comparable periods of maturity to
the loan maturity as of the fifteenth day of the month immediately preceding the month in which the
application for the extension of credit is received by the creditor; or
(2)
the total points and fees exceed: (i) 5% of the total loan amount if the loan amount is
$16,000 or greater, or (ii) $800 ifthe loan amount is less than $16,000.
However, "threshold loan" shall not include a loan that is made primarily for a business purpose
unrelated to the residential real property securing the loan and shall not include a loan with a total loan
amount over $250,000.
"Treasurer" means the Treasurer of Cook County.

SECTION 3 - COUNTY CONTRACTS
A.

The Chief Financial Officer shall determine whether any financial institution seeking a
contract with the County is a predatory lender as defined in this Ordinance. If the Chief
Financial Officer determines that any such financial institution is a predatory lender, the
County will not award a contract to such financial institution. For purposes of this
Ordinance, a County contract shall not include designation as a County depository. The
Chief Financial Officer shall notify the Treasurer of this determination.

B.

With each bid or offer submitted by a financial institution for any contract with the County,
there shall be a pledge signed by the chairman of the board, chief executive officer, or other
officer of the financial institution acceptable to the Chief Financial Officer. The pledge
shall be in substantially the following form:
We pledge that we are not and will not become a predatory lender as
defined in Cook County's Predatory Lending Ordinance. We further
pledge that none of our affiliates is, and none of them will become, a
predatory lender as defined in this Ordinance. We understand that
becoming a predatory lende.r or becoming an affiliate of a predatory lender
may result in the loss of the privilege of doing business with the County.

C.

Nothing in this Ordinance shall affect the validity of any contract entered into in connection
with any debt obligations issued by or on behalf of the County prior to a determination by
the Chief Financial Officer that an entity participating in the contract is a predatory lender.

1447

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

D.

The Chief Financial Officer, at the direction of the President of the Cook County Board of
Commissioners, may suspend the ineligibility of a financial institution in order to allow
execution of a contract with the financial institution upon written application by the head of
a County agency or department affected by the proposed contract setting forth facts
sufficient in the judgment of the purchasing agent to establish:

1.

that the public health, safety or welfare of the County requires the goods or services of
the financial institution; and

2.

that the County is unable to acquire the goods or services at comparable price and
quality, and in sufficient quantity, from other sources.

SECTION 4 - COUNTY DEPOSITORIES
A.

All financial institutions, seeking designation as a County depository by the Board of
Commissioners upon the request of the Treasurer, shall submit to the Chief Financial
Officer, prior to any such designation, a pledge affirming that neither it nor any of its
affiliates is or will become a predatory lender within the County. Upon receipt, the Chief
Financial Officer shall forward this pledge to the Treasurer. The pledge shall be signed by
the chairman of the board, chief executive officer, or other officer of the financial
institution acceptable to the Chief Financial Officer. The pledge shall be in substantially
the following form:
We pledge that we are not and will not become a predatory lender as
defined in this Ordinance. We further pledge that none of our affiliates
is, and none of them will become, a predatory lender as defined in this
Ordinance.
We understand that becoming a predatory lender or
becoming an affiliate of a predatory lender may result in the loss of our
designation as a County depository.

B.

Upon receipt of any written complaint regarding predatory lending practices by any
financial institution seeking designation as a County depository or serving as a County
depository, the Chief Financial Officer shall refer such complaints to the Treasurer who
wm may conduct an investigation of the complaint in accordance with the Treasurer's
policies and procedures.

SECTION 5 - SEVERABILITY
If any provision of this Ordinance is held invalid, such provision shall be deemed excised from
this Ordinance and the invalidity thereof shall not affect any of the other provisions of this Ordinance. If
the application of any provision of this Ordinance to any person or circumstance is held invalid, it shall
not affect the application of such provision to other persons or circumstances.

SECTION 6 - EFFECTIVE DATE
This Ordinance shall take effect 60 days after its passage and approval.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001 .
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

1488

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

241445

AN ORDINANCE DIRECTING COOK COUNTY TO ADOPT LEADERSHIP IN
ENERGY AND ENVIRONMENTAL DESIGN (LEED) GREEN BUILDING RATING
SYSTEM FOR ALL NEWLY CONSTRUCTED COUNTY FACILITIES (PROPOSED
ORDINANCE). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Mike Quigley, County
Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by William R. Moran and Herbert T. Schumann, County
Commissioners:
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the United States Green Building Council (USGBC), a non-profit, nationally
recognized association with membership representing all segments of the building industry,
including architects, manufacturers, government agencies, and environmentalists, has created
LEED, a green building rating system that provides specific principles and practices, some
mandatory but the majority discretionary, that may be applied during the design, construction,
and operation phases, which enable the building to be awarded points from reaching preset
standards of environmental efficiency so that it may achieve LEED certification from the
USGBC as a "green" building; and
THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED,
I.

That Cook County does hereby order all of its newly constructed buildings to employ
the LEED Green Building Rating System, Version 2.0, throughout their design,
construction, and operation and does further order that each new building must
achieve the LEED silver level of certification.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
II.

That the USGBC intends to release a revised version of the LEED Green Building
Rating System every three years; and with this in consideration when beginning a
new building project, Cook County shall refer to the most current version of the
LEED in existence; and after registering with the USGBC at the design stage of the
project as is required, the County may adhere to that existing version until completion
of the project, regardless of any new LEED version that may be released at a later
time.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
Ill.

That with specific regard to the LEED Energy and Atmosphere category, because
achieving increasing levels of energy performance above the set energy code
standards is the surest way of realizing significant operational cost savings, all
buildings must obtain a total of at least eight points.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
IV.

NOTE:

That Cook County also encourages the application of LEED principles during retrofit
and renovation projects of its current standing structures whenever it is practicable.
This matter was also referred to the Committee on Environmental Control. (See
Comm. No. 241446).

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated March 15, 2001:

revisions and additional construction administration services which were
necessary due to a delay in the completion of the project. The funds for these
services will be taken out of the liquidated damages which will be charged to the
contractor.

Commissioner Silvestri asked if liquidated damages will in fact be charged to the contractor?
Michael LaMont responded that the contractor is four months behind in completing the project and
contract provides for assessment of liquidated damages if the project is not completed on time. He further
stated that the contractor has no valid reason for not completing the project on time and damages are
being assessed.
Commissioner Silvestri asked if the facility is already complete?
Mr. LaMont stated that the facility is complete.
Commissioner Collins asked Mr. LaMont to clarify exactly how the liquidated damages will be recouped
by the County.
Mr. LaMont commented that the method to recoup liquidated damages is during the final contract
settlement where a deduction is made from the final payout. He said the only way the County can adjust
a contract is with Board approval, and concluded that the funds will be recovered through the amount
credited to the contractor for late performance.
Commissioner Sims asked ifthe damages could be recouped through errors and omissions?
Mr. LaMont answered that the damages could not be recovered through errors and omissions.
