Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Environmental Control of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant
to notice on Wednesday, April 11, 2001 at the hour of 10:30 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County
Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following item and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:

1494

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

241446

AN ORDINANCE DIRECTING COOK COUNTY TO ADOPT LEADERSHIP IN
ENERGY AND ENVIRONMENTAL DESIGN (LEED) GREEN BUILDING RA TING
SYSTEM FOR ALL NEWLY CONSTRUCTED COUNTY FACILITIES (PROPOSED
ORDINANCE). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Mike Quigley, County
Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by William R. Moran and Herbert T. Schumann, County
Commissioners:
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the United States Green Building Council (USGBC), a non-profit, nationally
recognized association with membership representing all segments of the building industry,
including architects, manufacturers, government agencies, and environmentalists, has created
LEED, a green building rating system that provides specific principles and practices, some
mandatory but the majority discretionary, that may be applied during the design, construction,
and operation phases, which enable the building to be awarded points from reaching preset
standards of environmental efficiency so that it may achieve LEED certification from the
USGBC as a "green" building; and
THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED,
I.

That Cook County does hereby order all of its newly constructed buildings to employ
the LEED Green Building Rating System, Version 2.0, throughout their design,
construction, and operation and does further order that each new building must
achieve the LEED silver level of certification.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
II.

That the USGBC intends to release a revised version of the LEED Green Building
Rating System every three years; and with this in consideration when beginning a
new building project, Cook County shall refer to the most current version of the
LEED in existence; and after registering with the USGBC at the design stage of the
project as is required, the County may adhere to that existing version until completion
of the project, regardless of any new LEED version that may be released at a later
time.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
III.

That with specific regard to the LEED Energy and Atmosphere category, because
achieving increasing levels of energy performance above the set energy code
standards is the surest way of realizing significant operational cost savings, all
buildings must obtain a total of at least eight points.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
IV.
NOTE:

That Cook County also encourages the application of LEED principles during retrofit
and renovation projects of its current standing structures whenever it is practicable.
This matter was also referred to the Committee on Construction. (See Comm.
No. 241445).

Chairman Moreno asked Commissioner Quigley to give background information regarding the proposed
ordinance.

1495

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
Commissioner Quigley commented about personal experiences during the first energy crisis when fewer
lights were used that year and smaller vehicles were purchased. He also said that same year the Gross
Nation.al Product (GNP) rose and energy consumption stayed the same. He stated that somewhere during
the l 970's through the 1990's, when OPEC released more oil and energy consumption rose, the U.S. lost
some lessons on energy savings.
Commissioner Quigley said today, when we hear of energy blackouts in California and of people in
Chicago who are unable to pay their heating bills, perhaps those lessons are coming back to us. He said
he thinks it is appropriate for government, particularly Cook County, to take a leadership role in moving
toward those energy efficiencies that were supposed to be learned some time ago.
The commissioner said the proposed ordinance stems from his visit to San Francisco, California that had
already passed a Green Building Ordinance that involved buildings the city built rather than buildings
outside of their jurisdiction. He stated the San Francisco ordinance did not follow the LEED standard, but
did give him the idea that Cook County should do something similar. He further said that discussions
with representatives of the Environmental Law and Policy Center focused on the Green Buildings Council
and the LEED's standard for buildings and building efficiency. Commissioner Quigley stated that the
LEED's standard not only covers building efficiency but also environmental qualities, orientations,
worker productivity, air quality and many other areas of concern to the County. He stated that the
ordinance is one way Cook County can take the lead in resolving energy efficiency problems.
The following speakers provided testimony on the proposed ordinance:
Helen Kessler, Executive Vice President, Sieben Energy Consultants
Karen J. Lewis, Environmental Law & Policy Center
Theodore P. Georgas, Chief Engineer, Cook County Highway Department
Chairman Moreno and Commissioner Silvestri asked to be listed as co-sponsors to the ordinance.
Chairman Moreno commented that he believes every commissioner is in favor of Cook County taking the
initiative on energy conservation and the environment; however, he said the county also needs to look at
the cost and maintenance associated with any new construction as it relates to the proposed ordinance.
Commissioner Silvestri stated that initially, new construction would probably cost more using the
standards in the proposed ordinance, but in the long run by approving the ordinance, taxpayer dollars will
be saved along with helping our children and the environment.
Commissioner Moran informed the subcommittee that he had recently attended a Department of Energy
Conference where the very same issue was discussed . The commissioner shared information regarding
Cook County's proposed ordinance at the meeting and was told that the possibility exists that a mandate
calling for all public buildings to conform to the LEED's example could become an unfunded mandate.
He said he supports the ordinance and Commissioner Quigley is on target with this proposal.
In response to comments made by Ted Georgios, Chief Engineer, Cook County Highway Department,
regarding a possible exemption to the ordinance for "no or low occupancy structures," Commissioner
Quigley stated that these structures should be exempt and he plans to make this a part of the proposed
ordinance. The commissioner further stated that the ordinance only applies to new buildings that will be
constructed after passage.
Chairman Moreno asked Michael LaMont, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy to give the
subcommittee an idea on how and where the county is moving on energy efficiency and this concept.

1496

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

Michael LaMont stated that the Office of Capital Planning and Policy has already considered energy
conservation and recycling as buildings are renovated and updated, particularly in the area of lighting. He
said that for the past five years, on retrofit projects, "green lights" have been successfully retrofitted in
various buildings. He further stated that the Office of Capital Planning and Policy is currently working
on the "Green Lights Fixture Replacement Project" that is more comprehensive, especially on the use of
energy efficient light fixtures. Mr. LaMont stated that the Board has already approved Phase I of the
project that includes outlying court buildings and Phase II includes all other buildings. He concluded by
stating that the Office will look at all criteria in the proposed ordinance as it relates to cost.
Commissioner Silvestri asked when the Office of Capital Planning and Policy will present a report to the
members.
Michael LaMont responded he plans to meet with staff, other county departments, and the Industrial
Engineers to thoroughly review the proposed ordinance. He concluded by stating that he will provide a
status report to the members within 30 to 60 days.
Vice Chairman Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Schumann, moved the deferral of
Communication No. 241446 until the Office of Capital Planning and Policy prepares a fiscal impact
statement. The motion carried.
Vice Chairman Silvestri moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Moran. The
motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.
Respectfully submitted,
COMMITTEE ON ENVIRONMENTAL CONTROL
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, Chairman
ATTEST: SANDRA K. WILLIAMS, Secretary
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Report of the Committee on
Environmental Control be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

242707

SHERIFF OF COOK COUNTY, Michael F. Sheahan, transmitting a Communication, dated
March 27, 2001:
Re: Appointment to the Cook County Emergency Telephone System Board
Respectfully requesting that Director JOHN KOZARITZ replace Deputy Chief Lombardo as
a member of the Cook County Emergency Telephone System Board (ETSB). Submitted is a
brief description of Director Kozaritz's credentials. Director Kozaritz has a long history of
Law Enforcement, and currently is the Director of the Sheriff's Communication Center. I
believe he will make a valuable contribution as a Board Member.
According to the by-laws of the ETSB, the Cook County Board of Commissioners must
approve all appointments to the Board. Please accept this letter as a formal nomination of

1498

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
242723

RESOLUTION SUPPORTING HOUSE BILL 2392 (PROPOSED RESOLUTION).
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Mike Quigley, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, many residential areas of Cook County are rapidly developing, as evidenced by
the recent construction of many new property developments, condominium units and
subdivisions throughout the County; and
WHEREAS, under current state law, a grantor may transfer ownership of a new residential
parcel to a grantee without providing a property index number (PIN) and in fact, many of
these newly built or newly divided properties are sold prior to assignment of proper property
index numbers by the Cook County Assessor; and
WHEREAS, the sale of parcels that have not yet been divided by the Cook County Assessor's
Office leads to imprecise billing of individual property owners, which can result in
overpayments, underpayments and penalties, creating confusion and frustration on the part of
these new homeowners; and
WHEREAS, the resulting confusion and frustration of these homeowners severely strains the
resources of the Cook County Assessor's Office and the Cook County Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, State Representatives Judy Erwin, Jim Brosnahan, Sara Feigenholtz, Julie
Harnos and the State Senator Christine Radogno have sponsored House Bill 2392, a bill only
affecting Cook County, which would require a grantor of property to provide the grantee with
an individual permanent index number that specifically represents that parcel of property
which that grantee has purchased; and
WHEREAS, House Bill 2392 also provides that if the permanent index number does not
represent the legal description of the property, the grantor may supply proof that he or she
either filed an application for division of the property with the Cook County Assessor's
Office, recorded a plat of subdivision, or recorded a condominium declaration; and
WHEREAS, a grantor's failure to meet these requirements will not invalidate the transaction,
but will render a grantor personally liable to grantee for any taxes and attorney's fees that may
be incurred until the requirements are met; and
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, the Cook County Assessor's Office and the Cook
County Board of Commissioners support this legislation, recently passed unanimously by the
House Judiciary I Committee.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby
urge the Illinois State Legislature to support this effort to facilitate the payment of accurate
property taxes by residential property owners in Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body, and a suitable copy of same be provided to the Illinois State Legislature.

In response to Commissioner Silvestri's request to hear from a representative of the Assessor's Office on
House Bill 2392, Terry Steczo stated the Assessor's Office is very supportive of the Resolution and House
Bill 2392.

1499

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
Mr. Steczo stated the intent of the bill is not only to ensure the proper conveyance and accuracy of
property records but also, to protect the county and purchasers of such property from the costly impact of
improper conveyances.
He explained the measure would require a developer to provide a Property Index Number (PIN) as
recorded with the legal description of the property, or to show proof that the application for division
petition for a separate PIN has been filed with the Assessor's Office.
Commissioner Silvestri requested information from Helen Haynes of the State's Attorney's Office, on the
feasibility of implementing and enforcing the measure pursuant to the County's home rule authority.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moran, moved the approval of Communication
No. 242723. The motion carried unanimously.

C.

SOLID WASTE MANAGEMENT
5.

SB 356 (Karpiel/Pankau)- Provides that an IEPA permit for a waste disposal facility
expires after 10 years if the facility has not received waste during such period and, at
the time of permitting, the facility was exempt from local siting approval.

In response to Commissioner Silvestri's request for further information, Steve Morrill stated that in 1987
Cook County approved special use zoning approval for a landfill in the Northwestern unincorporated area
of the county and the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency issued a permit. He explained that the
landfill question had been in the courts and just recently a US Supreme Court decision came down in
support of the authority of local agencies to proceed with such use. Mr. Morrill stated this bill was
introduced by individuals who were not happy with this decision and wish to stop the local agencies from
moving forward with the project.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved to oppose Item No. 6. The
motion carried unanimously.
D.

FOIA AND OPEN MEETINGS
6.

HB 2233 (Ruthorford/Burzynski) - Creates the Office of Public Records Access
Counsel within the Attorney General's Office to educate the public and public
bodies, and to issue advisory opinions, about access to public records. Also makes
mandatory a court's award of attorney's fees, costs and reasonable expenses to a
person who successfully challenges a public body's denial of access to public record.

7.

HB 3078 (Righter) - Specifies that financial amounts expended or collected by
public bodies in connection with settling threatened or actual litigation are public
information.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to receive and file Item Nos. 7
and 8. The motion carried unanimously.
9.

HB 3098 (Dart) - Requires a public body to keep verbatim minutes of any closed
meeting.

Commissioner Silvestri stated his concern, as Chairman of the Litigation Committee, that this bill could
hinder the members' ability to properly discuss matters in executive session.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to oppose Item No. 9.
motion carried.

1502

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

Commissioner Collins voted Present on Item No. 10.
11.

HB 543 (Righter/Cronin) - Increases the amount of time (from one to two years)
during which an action may be brought against a unit of local government or public
employee in connection with an injury or death arising out of patient care.

In response to Commissioner Lechowicz, Steve Morrill stated that the bill results from a recent decision
by the IL Supreme Court that affirmed the one-year time limitation for filings against public hospitals.
He explained the bill is drafted for the statutory change based on the dissenting opinion in this case.
Commissioner Lechowicz requested further information from Helen Haynes, of the State's Attorney's
Office, regarding past county cases. He asked for a comparison of the number of filings less than one
year and the estimated number beyond one year, including an estimated increase in costs the county might
face if this bill becomes law.

Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to receive and file Item No. 11.
The motion carried.
Commissioners Silvestri, Daley and Collins voted Present on Item No. 11.
F.

TOWNSHIPS
12.

HB 27 (Leitch) - Gives townships certain demolition authority, pursuant to
application with and order by a court, if a county first declines or fails to act on a
formal request by the township.

In response to Commissioner Daley's question, Steve Morrill stated the President opposed the measure as
currently drafted.
Commissioner Silvestri stated that since the county has no funding, beyond Community Development
Block Grants, to demolish buildings and therefore has limited use of this authority, he believes there
would be no negative impact on the county if this bill were to pass.
With leave of the committee, Chairman Hansen recognized Representative Skip Saviano.
Representative Saviano stated he had introduced similar legislation to House Bill 27 and is currently in
discussion with the President's office to come up with an agreed upon procedure, possibly using
intergovernmental agreements, when these matters arise. He noted that his legislation, House Bill 3007,
is also still pending in Springfield.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved to defer for 30 days Item
No. 12. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, Mary Kehoe Griffin, Chief Coordinator of the Bureau of Public Safety and Judicial
Coordination, is retiring from Cook County Government in April, 2001, with more than 30 years of
distinguished and dedicated service; and

1505

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
WHEREAS, Ms. Griffin received a Master of Social Work degree from Loyola University in Chicago
and began her career with County Government on July 1, 1970, in the Cook County Juvenile Court; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Griffin served for 10 years as the Assistant to the Chief Administrative Officer of the
Bureau of Administration, during which time she was responsible for many special projects with lasting
benefit to Cook County Government including developing Cook County's Employee Assistance Program,
and managing the establishment of the credit union services for County employees; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Griffin was the Program Coordinator for Cook County's hosting of NACo '93,
organizing all special events, activities, transportation, volunteers, and communications for the 5-day
national conference of 5,000 county officials; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Griffin devoted her management skills for two years as Assistant Superintendent and
Director of Programs and Planning at the Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center, being
responsible for educational, recreational and volunteer programs; and
WHEREAS, as Chief Coordinator of the Bureau of Public Safety and Judicial Coordination, Ms. Griffin
has continued her commitment to serving the citizens of Cook County by chairing committees such as the
Chicago Children Advocacy Center Strategic Planning Committee, the Domestic Violence Coordinating
Council Community Education Subcommittee and JOINT, the Job Opportunities for Individuals in Need
of Training Committee; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Griffin has been recognized by the community, having been awarded the "Anne O'Brien
Stevens Award" for outstanding contributions to the field of criminal justice for women in May, 2000, by
the Illinois Academy of Criminology, and "The Women in Justice Award" for her contributions as a role
model for women in criminal justice careers in October, 2000, by The Institute for Social Justice.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the Board
does hereby congratulate Mary Kehoe Griffin for her 31 years of dedicated service and extend to her best
wishes for a happy, healthy retirement; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be presented to Mary Kehoe
Griffin in honor of her outstanding contribution and service to Cook County Government.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.

01-R-259
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
BLUE BOW CAMPAIGN
CHILD ABUSE PREVENTION MONTH

Whereas, child abuse prevention is a Countywide problem and finding solutions depends on involvement
among people throughout the county, including the court system; and
Whereas, in Cook County alone for Fiscal Year 2000 there were 40, 73 7 reported cases of child abuse and
neglect; and
Whereas, the effects of child abuse are felt Countywide and need to be addressed by the entire County;
and
Whereas, effective child abuse prevention programs succeed because of partnerships created among the
county, the courts, social service agencies, schools, religious organizations, law enforcement agencies,
and the business community; and
·Whereas, Parents Care & Share, a prevention program offering positive alternatives to help break the
cycle of abuse, is sponsoring the Illinois Blue Bow Campaign to heighten awareness of the need to
support families; and
Whereas, all residents of Cook County should become more aware of child abuse and its prevention and
to become involved in supporting parents to raise their children in a safe, nurturing environment.
Now, Therefore, Be It Resolved, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby affirm its
commitment to building strong, healthy families in Cook County and to fostering intergovernmental
cooperation in hopes of finding solutions to the continuing problem of child abuse and neglect.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Carr, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 20, 2001 from
JAMES L. ELDRIDGE, JR., Chief Administrative Officer, Bureau of Administration
Respectfully request the adoption of this resolution and authorization to notify the Office of the Governor
of the County's intent to retain its bond volume cap for various housing and economic development
purposes.
The County of Cook must adopt a resolution to retain $5,633,312.50 in private activity bonds no later
than April 30, 2001. Failure to adopt such a resolution and notification to the Office of the Governor
would result in forfeiture of the bond cap to the State.
01-R-261
RESOLUTION
Concerning 2001 Bond Volume Cap

WHEREAS, the County of Cook, Illinois (the "County") is a home rule unit under Subsection (a) of
Section 6, Article VII of the Illinois Constitution of 1970; and
WHEREAS, there exists within the borders of the County a recognized need for decent, well-constructed
and maintained affordable housing and the need for lower cost financing of business expansion to create
and retain jobs; and
WHEREAS, the County is authorized under state law and the County's home rule powers (i) to issue
revenue bonds ("Bonds") to finance below market interest rate mortgage loans to individuals and to
finance below market interest rate loans to businesses and other organizations to encourage the creation
and retention of jobs and (ii) to issue mortgage credits certificates ("Certificates") to provide housing
assistance for qualified individuals; and
WHEREAS, the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended (the "Code") limits the amount of Bonds
and Certificates that may be issued by the County on a tax-exempt basis under the Code; and
WHEREAS, the County, by previous resolution, has ceded $1,000,000.00 of its Private Activity Bond
Volume Cap to the Illinois Housing Development Authority in relation to a multifamily housing project;
and
WHEREAS, the County desires to consider establishing and implementing 2001 Bond and Certificate
programs with the allocation of its 2001 bond volume cap as defined in Section 146 of the Code (the
"Volume Cap") in the remaining amount of$5,633,312.50; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to the Illinois Private Activity Bond Allocation Act (the "Act"), the County's
Volume Cap allocation may be ceded to the State of Illinois if it is not used or allocated to specific
projects or purposes by April 30, 2001.

1509

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and the Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, Illinois ("Corporate Authorities"):
Section 1. Public Purpose. It is hereby found, determined and declared that the purpose of this
Resolution is to take steps designed to reduce the cost of financing principal residences located in the
County in order to provide decent, affordable housing for qualifying persons of low and moderate
income; and to provide below market interest rate loans to businesses and other organizations to create
and retain jobs.
Section 2. Allocation of Volume Cap. The Corporate Authorities hereby authorize the allocation of the
entire amount of the County's Volume Cap for calendar year 2001 to a Single Family Mortgage Bond, a
Mortgage Credit Certificate Program, an Industrial Revenue Bond Program, multi family housing
projects, any purpose allowed under the code, or any combination thereof, to be approved by the
Corporated Authorities.
Section 3. Approval of Further Actions. From and after the adoption of this Resolution, the proper
officials, agents and employees of the County are hereby authorized, empowered and directed to do all
such acts and things and to execute all such documents as may be necessary to carry out and comply with
the provisions of this Resolution or to effectuate the purpose hereof.
Section 4. Effective Date. This Resolution shall be in full force and effect upon its passage and approval.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001 .
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

01-R-262
RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 6b which provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for an industrial facility;
and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the approval by the County Board of a special exception for abandonment
in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive months upon
purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from
Gullo International Development Corp. and the Resolution of the Village of Elk Grove Village for a
vacant industrial facility located at 2200-20 Arthur Avenue in Elk Grove Village, Elk Grove Township,
Cook County, Property Index Numbers 08-35-301-043-0000, 08-35-403-052-0000, 08-35-403-053-0000,
08-35-056-0000, and 08-35-403-065-0000; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the granting of a 6b Real
Estate Classification to Gullo International Development Corp. will be beneficial to the County; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for 18 months at the time of purchase, that special circumstances are present and that this incentive is
necessary for the productive reuse of the building to occur.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the County
of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners support and consent to the
application of Gullo International Development Corp. for a facility located at 2200-20 Arthur Avenue in
Elk Grove Village, Elk Grove Township, Cook County under the provision of Class 6b abatement
incentive for abandonment of Jess than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

leader, Yosef Yitzchok Schneerson, sent emissaries to the United States. In 1940, Rabbi Shusterman
joined the Lubavitch Yeshiva, where he was ordained, and
WHEREAS, Rabbi Hershel Shusterman came to Chicago in 1947 to lead Congregation Agudas
Chabad and in 1959 he joined the 104-year-old Congregation Bnei Ruven. Rabbi Shusterman
spearheaded the relocation of the Bnei Ruven synagogue from the West Side of Chicago to West Rogers
Park, and
WHEREAS, Rabbi Hershel Shusterman possessed a depth of knowledge of Jewish law that made him
a respected arbitrator to religious communities worldwide. As the senior rabbi in the Lubavitcher Hasidic
sect of Orthodox Judaism, Rabbi Shusterman advised both rabbis and lay people on Jewish law issues.
Rabbi Daniel Moscowitz, regional director of Lubavitch Chabad Illinois described Rabbi Shusterman as
"a rabbi's rabbi", having both well-versed knowledge and understanding, and

help", and
WHEREAS, Rabbi Hershel Shusterman and his wife established an interest-free loan account to aid
needy people in the Lubavitch community. Since it's inception on the early 1970s, more than half-amillion dollars has been loaned, and
WHEREAS, Rabbi Hershel Shusterman devoted his life to his family, his synagogue, the Lubavitch
community, and his faith.

and the University of Minnesota. Mr. Weinberg was chairmen of the sociology and anthropology
department at Roosevelt University, and joined Loyola University-Chicago where he remained as
professor emeritus after his retirement, and
WHEREAS, Samuel K. Weinberg was recognized by The National Science Foundation as one of the
"outstanding members of the profession". He also served as co-chairman of the Advisory Council on
Juvenile Delinquency for the Cook County Sheriff, and
WHEREAS, Samuel K. Weinberg wrote eight books and many articles focusing on society's voiceless
and forgotten people. He championed the homeless and mentally ill by writing about their plight, and
became an internationally recognized authority on social issues, and

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst,
DONALD E. WRIGHT
WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright was the beloved husband of (the late) Verna, adoring father of Amy,
Sara and John, loving brother of Verna, Marie, Ethel and Wilbur, proud grandfather of one grandchild,
and affectionate uncle of several nieces and nephews, and
WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright received a Bachelor of Arts degree in English from the University of
Colorado and a Master's Degree in library science from the University of Denver. Mr. Wright embarked
on a lifelong passion for reading and became an assistant librarian with the Illinois State Library in 1965,
and
WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright became the Director of the Evanston Public Library in 1967. He
dedicated much of his efforts to modernizing the library system and paving the road for a new library
building. In 1980, Mr. Wright implemented a computerized public access catalog with touch-screen
terminals for library patrons. The Evanston Public Library is believed to be the first library in Illinois to
have instituted such a system, and
WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright championed a new building for the Evanston Public Library, seeking
community recognition and support. Mr. Wright retired from the library in 1992, shortly after an
architect for the new library was chosen through a design competition. Mr. Wright joined architectural
experts and community representatives in selecting the winning design, and
WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright was a longstanding member of the American Library Association where
he served in various leadership roles, and helped develop a publication that provides support for small
libraries, and
WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright also served as an interim library administrator for the Niles Public
Library District from 1992 until 1993, and the interim director of the Oak Park Public Library in 1996,
and

1525

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright was chairman of the Illinois delegation to the first White House
Conference on Libraries during the Carter administration, and
WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright was a person of deep faith, being an ordained elder with Northminster
Presbyterian Church in Evanston. Mr. Wright was also a past president of the Rotary Club, and
WHEREAS, Donald E. Wright was devoted to his family, single-handedly caring for his children after
the death of his wife in 1983. Mr. Wright left a legacy of passion for books and learning, community
service, faith and devotion, and love for his family.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Donald E. Wright, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
family in their hour of sorrow and joins his family in honoring his memory, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family of
Donald E. Wright as a memorial of his good works and spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

01-R-277
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TED LECHOWICZ, PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
AND JOHN P. DALEY, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the 210th Anniversary of the adoption of the Constitution of Poland will be
celebrated on May 3, 2001; and

1530

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
WHEREAS, the people of the County of Cook celebrate this most special occasion with civic and
religious events; and
WHEREAS, the Polish Constitution was the first on the European continent to establish a
democratic government and was modeled after the Constitution of the United States adopted only two
years earlier; and
WHEREAS, the Polish people were able to achieve individual freedom and political
independence without resorting to bloody revolution or civil insurrection; and
WHEREAS, the symbol of the Constitution kept alive the spirit of freedom even after the country
of Poland was partitioned among Russia, Prussia, and Austria for all of the 19th century and for the early
part of the 20th century and after Poland later suffered under the domination of the old Soviet Union
during the period of the Cold War; and
WHEREAS, the people of Poland and the people of the United States share a common heritage of
respect for freedom and liberty; and
WHEREAS, the people of Poland have contributed to the greatness of the United States through
the great efforts of many, as epitomized by Thaddeus Kosciuzko, who selected the site of and designed
the United States Military Academy at West Point, and General Casimir Pulaski, who fought and died
valiantly in the Revolutionary War oflndependence; and
WHEREAS, the people of Poland once again are living in freedom and have led other peoples to
break free of authoritarian governments that once ruled them; and
WHEREAS, the Polish Constitution of 1791 will forever stand as a banner for the long struggle
for freedom for people throughout the history of the world and serves as a reminder that freedom can be
protected with unceasing vigilance and effort.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that we offer our sincere appreciation to the Polish
people for their efforts on behalf of freedom, efforts that have truly changed the world; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that we congratulate the people of Poland on the 210th
Anniversary of the May 3rd Polish Constitution, a document that kept the struggle for freedom alive in
Poland and that serves as a symbol of liberty and justice for people throughout the world; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that suitable copies of this Resolution be presented to Mr.
Edward Moskal, President of the PNA, and Mr. Wallace Ozog, President of the PRCUA, as a measure of
our respect for the people of Poland and their great accomplishments as represented by the Polish
Constitution of May 3, 1791 .
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, the County Board has learned with sorrow of the death of Richard J. Towalski, a
long-time prominent Polish entertainer in the Chicagoland area; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Towalski entertained the people of Chicagoland for 46 years, beginning at the
age of 12 by performing in polka bands; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Towalski was a versatile musician, playing the concertina, accordion, drums
and trumpet, as well as singing; and
WHEREAS, in 1969 Mr. Towalski was proclaimed "Polka General of Chicago" by the
Honorable Richard J. Daley, Mayor of Chicago; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Towalski was twice named songwriter of the year by the United Polka
Association, first in 1977, and then again 21 years later in 1998; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Towalski also hosted a regular radio show (broadcast on WSBC-AM 1240 in
Chicago and on WCFJ-AM 1470 in Chicago Heights); and
WHEREAS, Mr. Towalski was a fixture in the Polish-American community of Cook County for
many years; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Towalski leaves to cherish his memory his fiance, Marsha Bartus, his mother,
Jeanette Towalski, his brother, Joseph Towalski, and many other family members and friends; and
WHEREAS, the "Polka General" will be missed by all who knew him.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
does hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Richard J. Towalski, offers its heartfelt sympathy to
his family in their hour of sorrow and loneliness, for their loss is shared by all Members of this Body and
the people of the County of Cook, and join his family and friends in honoring his memory.

1532

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

their children; and

center of American families; and
WHEREAS, children should be nurtured and invested in to preserve and enhance economic prosperity,
democracy, and the American spirit; and
WHEREAS, families should be encouraged to engage in family and community activities that include
extended and elderly family members and encourage children to explore, develop confidence and pursue
their dreams; and
WHEREAS, Latinos in the United States continue the tradition of honoring their children on this day and
wish to share this custom with the rest of the nation; and

1534

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

WHEREAS, the designation of a day of special recognition of children of the United States will provide
an opportunity to children to reflect on their future, to articulate their dreams and aspirations, and find
comfort and security in the support of their family members and communities; and
WHEREAS, the National Latino Children's Institute, serving as a voice for children, has worked with
cities across the country to declare April 30, 2001 as "Dia de los Ninos: Celebrating Young Americans", a
day to bring together Latinos and other communities nationwide to celebrate and uplift children.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby designate April 30, 2001 as "Dia de los Ninos: Celebrating Young Americans" in Cook County
and encourage the residents of Cook County to join with all children, families, organizations,
communities, and churches to observe the day with appropriate events; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body and that a suitable copy of it be tendered to the National Latino Children's Institute.

Mexican state of Durango who now reside in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Durango Unido is an initiative of political and religious leaders, professionals, business
groups and individuals who felt the need to unite and resolve the many social, economic and educational
problems that face residents from Durango both in Mexico and in the U.S.; and
WHEREAS, Durango Unido also seeks to promote the individual culture, customs and family values of
Durango so as to maintain the identity of Durango residents .and their children; and

1535

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
WHEREAS, among the many endeavors embarked on by Durango Unido includes the ongoing
collection of funds and donations to provide medical equipment and supplies to impoverished towns in
the state of Durango, as well as hosting an official visit by Durango Governor Angel Sergio Guerrero
Mier to Chicago in 1999 that included a town meeting at Douglas Park attended by hundreds of Durango
residents from across Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Durango Unido will be celebrating its 5th Anniversary on April 21, 2001, with a gala event
to be held at the Chantilly Banquet, in LaGrange, Illinois.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby congratulate Durango Unido en Chicago on its 5th year of providing progress and empowerment
to Durango residents, both in Mexico and in the U.S.; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceeding of this Honorable
Body and that a suitable copy of same be tendered to Jesus Saenz, president of Durango Unido en
Chicago, as a memento of the honor bestowed upon them on this day.

01-R-283
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE MIKE QUIGLEY, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by

HE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI,
DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE AND
CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst;

1537

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

CHARLIESOO
WHEREAS, Charlie Soo spent the last two decades tirelessly working to improve the lives of others;
and
WHEREAS, Charlie Soo came to Chicago as a Chinese immigrant in the 1970s and soon thereafter
began rallying support to improve neighborhood conditions along Argyle Street, where he later became
known as the unofficial "Mayor of Argyle"; and
WHEREAS, Charlie Soo worked diligently with the police, city officials, and local merchants to make
changes within the community that led to safer streets and thriving commerce along Argyle Street in the
area now known as "New Chinatown"; and
WHEREAS, within the New Chinatown community, Charlie Soo sought to celebrate diversity and
promote unity; and
WHEREAS, as founder and director of the Asian American Small Business Association, Charlie Soo
helped foster economic development among the restaurants and storefronts along Argyle Street; and
WHEREAS, Charlie Soo worked with local businesses to organize the annual "Taste of Argyle" food
festival that has been going on since 1991; and
WHEREAS, Charlie Soo had no blood relatives in Chicago but his selfless efforts to improve the lives
and opportunities of the people of New Chinatown endeared him to the hearts of all in the community.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Charlie Soo, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his friends
and constituents in their hour of sorrow, and joins them in honoring his memory; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the Asian
American Small Business Association as a memorial of his good works and spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, Wetau Haley Barsh has been a dedicated enthusiastic employee of Chicago Public schools
for over 40 years. She is the wife of James Edward Brash and mother of James Wendell Barsh; and
WHEREAS, Mrs. Barsh received her Bachelors or Science, in Business Administration from Tennessee
State University (1961), Master of Arts in Early Education from Governors State University (1975), and
Associate Degree in Computer Science from Olive Harvey City College (1975); and
WHEREAS, Mrs. Barsh has served as Team Leader for Technology Grants, Department Chairperson,
Academic Chairperson, Technology Coordinator and language arts teacher at Marcus Garvey Elementary
School. She has set an outstanding example for her colleagues and students since 1973 and will retire on
June 13, 2001; and
WHEREAS, Sister Barsh has been active in a variety of fraternal and civic organizations, such as Alpha
Kappa Alpha Sorority, Inc., Order of Eastern Star, State of Illinois, Prince Hall Affiliation, American
Investment Club and the Holy Name of Mary Catholic Church and will be honored by her friends and
family on May 4, 2001 at a recognition dinner; and
WHEREAS, it is the custom of the Cook County Board of Commissioners to recognize and congratulate
the exemplary works of its' citizens.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that We, the Members of the Cook County Board
congratulate Wetau Haley Barsh on the occasion of her retirement and wish her good health, happiness
and long life; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Mrs. Wetau
Haley Barsh and also spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Honoring Glenview Trustee Kent B. Fuller
WHEREAS, Kent B. Fuller is retiring from the Village of Glenview's Board of Trustees after 12
years of service on the board; and
WHEREAS, Kent B. Fuller was first elected to the Board of Trustees in 1989; and
WHEREAS, prior to his service to the Board of Trustees, Kent B. Fuller served on the Glenview
Library Board from 1968 to 1989; and
WHEREAS, Kent B. Fuller served as Chairman of the Planning Commission from 1977 to 1984;
and
WHEREAS, in addition to Kent B. Fuller's service to the Village of Glenview he has also
demonstrated his sincere love of the outdoors in both his chosen profession and in his numerous volunteer
efforts; and
WHEREAS, Kent B. Fuller has demonstrated a professional commitment to the environment in
his service to the United State Environmental Protection Agency.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
congratulate Kent B. Fuller for his excellence and commitment to the Village of Glenview and his
continued service to the health and well being of the area's natural assets; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be presented to Kent B.
Fuller and be spread upon the proceedings of this Honorable Body.

Ol-R-287
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Co-sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI,
DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Whereas, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has taken from our midst;
Pastor Joseph Wells
profound gospel minister and former Pastor of the Mount Pisgah Missionary Baptist Church of Chicago
where he served for over 55 years; and
Whereas, Pastor Wells was ordained as a minister in 1939 and as a Biblical scholar, he attended Moody
Bible Institute and the Billips Theological Seminary. In 1975, an Honorary Divinity Degree, from
Hamilton State University in Tucson, Arizona, was conferred upon him for outstanding leadership; and
Whereas, as a visionary, Pastor Wells and the Mount Pisgah congregation the first Black church in
Chicago to use radio programming to minister to the sick, shut-in and those unable to attend regular
church services. Years later, in 1988, another milestone was made when church services were televised
on a cable network station; and

1542

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

Whereas, one of the many highlights of Pastor Wells' Ministerial career was his visit to the Holy Land
where he was baptized in the River of Jordan; and
Whereas, as one who deeply subscribed to scripture, in May 1981, Pastor Wells established the Mount
Pisgah Food for the Hungry Foundation, Inc. that has helped provide more than 4 million healthy and
hearty bags of groceries to the less fortunate; and
Whereas, in 1990, Pastor Wells was honored with a civic and ministerial salute and the 4600 block of Dr.
Martin Luther King, Jr. Drive was renamed "Reverend Joseph Wells Drive"; and
Whereas, Pastor Wells was a respected member of the clergy and one of the founding ministers of the
"Broadcast Ministers' Alliance and the "Illinois National State Convention" serving in various capacities.
Now, Therefore, Be It Resolved, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners expresses to the family
of Pastor Joseph Wells their Sadness and offer their deepest condolences; and
Be It Further Resolved, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be prepared and presented to the family
of Pastor Wells as a memorial of his contribution to every aspect of the community.

Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the County Auditor be directed to audit the checking accounts of said

1595

* ** * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 16, 200 I from
DOROTHY BROWN, Clerk of the Circuit Court
The Resolution requests that the following names be added and deleted as authorized signatories for the
subsequent investment account maintained by the Office of the Clerk of the Circuit Court.
01-R-340
RESOLUTION

WHEREAS the Cook County Board of Commissioners has the legal authority to authorize its
departments and offices to open and maintain investment accounts at various banks; and
WHEREAS it is now necessary to update those persons who are authorized to be signatories on these
investment accounts.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED that the investment account at Associated Bank, for the
following purposes indicated, be updated for the Clerk of the Circuit Court's Certificate of Deposit
Account.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the following are the names as signers of the aforesaid investment
account be deleted:
Aurelia Pucinski

George Rada

Ronald J. Banks

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the following are the names of those persons who shall be authorized
to sign on this investment account.
Dorothy Brown
Squire Lance
Laura Lane Ferguson

Clerk of the Circuit Court of Cook County
Executive Clerk/Public Policy
Executive Clerk/Operations and Administration

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the County Auditor be directed to audit the investment account of
said institution at the close of each Fiscal Year or anytime it see fit, and to file report(s) thereon with the
Cook County Board.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 200 I.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

* ** * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 16, 2001 from
DOROTHY BROWN, Clerk of the Circuit Court
The Resolution requests that the following names be added and deleted as authorized signatories for the
subsequent investment account maintained by the Office of the Clerk of the Circuit Court.
01-R-356
RESOLUTION

WHEREAS the Cook County Board of Commissioners has the legal authority to authorize its
departments and offices to open and maintain investment accounts at various banks; and
WHEREAS it is now necessary to update those persons who are authorized to be signatories on these
investment accounts.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED that the investment account at LaSalle Bank N.A., for the
following purposes indicated, be updated for the Clerk of the Circuit Court's Certificate of Deposit
Account.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the following are the names as signers of the aforesaid investment
account be deleted:
Aurelia Pucinski

George Rada

Ronald J. Banks

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the following are the names of those persons who shall be authorized
to sign on this investment account.
Dorothy Brown
Squire Lance
Laura Lane Ferguson

Clerk of the Circuit Court of Cook County
Executive Clerk/Public Policy
Executive Clerk/Operations and Administration

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the County Auditor be directed to audit the investment account of
said institution at the close of each Fiscal Year or anytime it see fit, and to file report(s) thereon with the
Cook County Board.
Approved and adopted this 17th day of April 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

1620

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001
PUBLIC TESTIMONY

Pursuant to Rule 4-30, Jasmine Salgado, a member of the Blocks Together Organization, addressed the
President and Members of the Cook County Board. Ms. Salgado expressed support for a health care
clinic in Garfield Park and Humboldt Park.

* * * * *
Pursuant to Rule 4-30, Ida Hernandez, a member of the Blocks Together Organization, addressed the
President and Members of the Cook County Board. Ms. Hernandez expressed support for a health care
clinic in Garfield Park and Humboldt Park.

* * * * *
Pursuant to Rule 4-30, Heather Hastings, of the Affordable Housing Committee, addressed the President
and Members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners. Ms. Hastings expressed concern regarding
property tax assessments and further voiced her support for the Cook County Longtime Homeowner
Property Tax Assessment Exemption Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Commissioner Maldonado.

* * * * *
Pursuant to Rule 4-30, Maria Romero, of the Affordable Housing Committee, addressed the President and
Members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners. Ms. Romero expressed concern regarding
property tax assessments and further voiced her support for the Cook County Longtime Homeowner
Property Tax Assessment Exemption Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Commissioner Maldonado.

* * * * *
Pursuant to Rule 4-30, Silvia Nebel, of West Town Leadership United (WTLU), addressed the President
and Members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners. Ms. Nebel expressed concern regarding
property tax assessments and further voiced her support for the Cook County Longtime Homeowner
Property Tax Assessment Exemption Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Commissioner Maldonado.

* * * * *
Pursuant to Rule 4-30, Lee Robbins, of Allstate Insurance, addressed the President and Members of the
Cook County Board of Commissioners. Mr. Robbins expressed concern regarding property tax
assessments and further voiced his support for the Cook County Longtime Homeowner Property Tax
Assessment Exemption Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Commissioner Maldonado.

* * ** *
Pursuant to Rule 4-30, Joel Monarch, a resident of Chicago, addressed the President and Members of the
Cook County Board of Commissioners. Mr. Monarch expressed concern regarding property tax
assessments and further voiced his support for the Cook County Longtime Homeowner Property Tax
Assessment Exemption Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Commissioner Maldonado.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 17, 2001

ADJOURNMENT
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Goslin, moved that the meeting do now adjourn to
meet again at the same time and same place on Tuesday, May 1, 2001, in accordance with County Board
Resolution Ol-R-12.
